*bus, unsigned int val);\n707: /*\n708:  * Interface for HD codec\n709:  */\n710: \n711: /*\n712:  * CORB / RIRB interface\n713:  */\n714: static int azx_alloc_cmd_io(struct azx *chip)\n715: {\n716: 0;\n2077: }\n2078: \n2079: /* get the current DMA position with correction on VIA chips */\n2080: static unsigned int azx_via_get_position(struct azx *chip,\n2081: \t\t\t\t\t struct azx_dev azx_dev->bufsize + link_pos - fifo_size;\n2115: \telse\n2116: \t\tmini_pos = link_pos - fifo_size;\n2117: \n2118: \t/* Find nearest previous boudary */\n2119: \tmod_mini_pos = mini_pos % azx_dev->period_bytes;\n2120: \tmod_link_pos = link_pos % azx_dev->period_bytes;\n2121: \tif (mod_link_pos >= fifo_size)\n2122: \t\tbound_pos = link_pos - mod_link_pos;\n2123: \telse if (mod_dma_pos >= mod_mini_pos)\n2124: \t\tbound_pos = mini_pos - mod_mini_pos;\n2125: \telse {\n2126: \t\tbound_pos = mini_pos - mod_mini_pos + azx_dev->period_bytes;\n2127: \t\tif (bound_pos >= azx_get_position(struct azx *chip,\n2136: \t\t\t\t     struct azx_dev *azx_dev,\n2137: \t\t\t\t     bool with_check)\n2138: {\n2139: \tunsigned int pos;\n2140: \tint stream = azx_dev->substream->stream;\n2141: \n2142: \tswitch (chip->position_fix[stream]) {\n2143: \tcase POS_FIX_LPIB:\n2144: \t\t/* read LPIB */\n2145: \t\tpos = azx_sd_readl(azx_dev, SD_LPIB);\n2146: \t\tbreak;\n2147: \tcase POS_FIX_VIACOMBO:\n2148: \t\tpos = azx_via_get_position(chip, azx_dev);\n2149: \t\tbreak;\n2150: \tdefault:\n2151: \t\t/* use the position buffer */\n2152: \t\tpos = le32_to_cpu(*azx_dev->posbuf);\n2153: \t\tif (with_check && chip->position_fix[stream] == POS_FIX_AUTO) {\n2154: \t\t\tif (!pos || pos == (u32)-1) {\n2155: \t\t\t\tprintk(KERN_WARNING\n2156: \t\t\t\t       \"hda-intel: Invalid position buffer, \"\n2157: \t\t\t\t       \"using LPIB read method instead.\\n\");\n2158: \t\t\t\tchip->position_fix[stream] = POS_FIX_LPIB;\n2159: \t\t\t\tpos = azx_sd_readl(azx_dev, SD_LPIB);\n2160: \t\t\t} else\n2161: \t\t\t\tchip->position_fix[stream] = POS_FIX_POSBUF;\n2162: \t\t}\n2163: \t\tbreak;\n2164: \t}\n2165: \n2166: \tif (pos >= azx_dev->bufsize)\n2167: \t\tpos = 0;\n2168: \n2169: \t/* calculate runtime delay from LPIB */\n2170: \tif (azx_dev->substream->runtime &&\n2171: \t    chip->position_fix[stream] == POS_FIX_POSBUF &&\n2172: \t    (chip->driver_caps & AZX_DCAPS_COUNT_LPIB_DELAY)) {\n2173: \t\tunsigned int lpib_pos = azx_sd_readl(azx_dev, SD_LPIB);\n2174: \t\tint delay;\n2175: \t\tif (stream == SNDRV_PCM_STREAM_PLAYBACK)\n2176: \t\t\tdelay = pos - lpib_pos;\n2177: \t\telse\n2178: \t\t\tdelay = lpib_pos - pos;\n2179: \t\tif (delay < 0)\n2180: \t\t\tdelay += azx_dev->bufsize;\n2181: \t\tif (delay >= azx_dev->period_bytes) {\n2182: \t\t\tsnd_printk(KERN_WARNING SFX\n2183: \t\t\t\t   \"Unstable LPIB (%d >= %d); \"\n2184: \t\t\t\t   \"disabling LPIB delay counting\\n\",\n2185: \t\t\t\t \t\t\tbytes_to_frames(azx_dev->substream->runtime, delay);\n2191: \t}\n2192: \treturn pos;\n2193: }\n2194: \n2195: static snd_pcm_uframes_t azx_pcm_pointer(struct snd_pcm_substream *substream)\n2196: {\n2197: \tstruct azx_pcm *apcm = snd_pcm_substream_chip(substream);\n2198: \tstruct azx *chip = apcm->chip;\n2199: \tstruct azx_dev *azx_dev = get_azx_dev(substream);\n2200: \treturn bytes_to_frames(substream->runtime,\n2201: \t\t\t       azx_get_position(chip, azx_dev, false));\n2202: }\n2203: \n2204: /*\n2205:  * Check whether the current DMA position is acceptable for updating\n2206:  * periods.  Returns non-zero if it's OK.\n2207:  *\n2208:  * Many HD-audio controllers appear pretty inaccurate about\n2209:  * the update-IRQ timing.  The IRQ is issued before actually the\n2210:  * data is processed.  So, we need to process it afterwords in a\n2211:  * workqueue.\n2212:  */\n2213: static int azx_position_ok(struct azx *chip, struct azx_dev *azx_dev)\n2214: {\n2215: \tu32 wallclk;\n2216: \tunsigned int pos;\n2217: \tint stream;\n2218: \n2219: \twallclk = azx_readl(chip, WALLCLK) - azx_dev->start_wallclk;\n2220: \tif (wallclk < (azx_dev->period_wallclk * 2) / 3)\n2221: \t\treturn -1;\t/* bogus (too early) interrupt */\n2222: \n2223: \tstream = azx_dev->substream->stream;\n2224: \tpos = azx_get_position(chip, azx_dev, true);\n2225: \n2226: \tif (WARN_ONCE(!azx_dev->period_bytes,\n2227: \t\t      \"hda-intel: zero azx_dev->period_bytes\"))\n2228: \t\treturn -1; /* this shouldn't happen! */\n2229: \tif (wallclk < (azx_dev->period_wallclk * 5) / 4 &&\n2230: \t    pos % azx_dev->period_bytes > azx_dev->period_bytes / 2)\n2231: \t\t/* NG - it's below the first next period boundary */\n2232: \t\treturn bdl_pos_adj[chip->dev_index] ? 0 : -1;\n2233: \tazx_dev->start_wallclk += wallclk;\n2234: \treturn 1; /* OK, it's fine */\n2235: }\n2236: \n2237: /*\n2238:  * The work for pending PCM period updates.\n2239:  */\n2240: static void azx_irq_pending_work(struct work_struct *work)\n2241: {\n2242: \tstruct azx *chip = container_of(work, struct azx, irq_pending_work);\n2243: \tint i, pending, ok;\n2244: \n2245: \tif (!chip->irq_pending_warned) {\n2246: \t\tprintk(KERN_WARNING\n2247: \t\t       \"hda-intel: IRQ timing workaround is activated \"\n2248: \t\t       \"for card #%d. Now I see the azx_init_chip function. The key part is at line 1211-1212 where it checks if chip->initialized is already true and returns early if so. This is a problem! \n\nLooking at the azx_resume function (line 2539-2566), I see that it calls azx_init_chip(chip, 1) at line 2561. However, if chip->initialized is already 1, then azx_init_chip will return immediately without doing anything!\n\nThe problem is that in azx_resume, the chip->initialized flag is never reset before calling azx_init_chip. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_019eHaHsc6AVAAJfZP91P583","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the issue! The azx_init_cmd_io function sets up the CORB (Command Output Ring Buffer) and RIRB (Response Input Ring Buffer) registers. This is critical for codec communication.\n\nLooking at the azx_resume function:\n1. It calls pci_restore_state() and pci_enable_device()\n2. It calls azx_init_pci() to clear TCSEL and enable snoop\n3. It calls azx_init_chip(chip, 1) which is supposed to reinitialize the chip\n\nHowever, the problem is in azx_init_chip():\n```c\nstatic void azx_init_chip(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n{\n\tif (chip->initialized)\n\t\treturn;  // <-- THIS IS THE BUG!\n\t\n\t// reset controller\n\tazx_reset(chip, full_reset);\n\t\n\t// initialize interrupts\n\tazx_int_clear(chip);\n\tazx_int_enable(chip);\n\t\n\t// initialize the codec command I/O\n\tif (!chip->single_cmd)\n\t\tazx_init_cmd_io(chip);\n\t\n\t// ... more initialization ...\n\t\n\tchip->initialized = 1;\n}\n```\n\nThe bug is that if chip->initialized is already 1 (which it will be on second or subsequent resume calls), the function returns immediately without doing any of the reinitialization work. This means the CORB/RIRB is not reinitialized, which could be causing the codec communication issues.\n\nAdditionally, looking at the azx_free_cmd_io function (line 970-977), I notice that on suspend, the function at line 954 calls azx_free_cmd_io() which disables the CORB and RIRB. But this doesn't clear the chip->initialized flag!\n\nSo the sequence is:\n1. First suspend: azx_free_cmd_io() disables CORB/RIRB, but chip->initialized remains 1\n\n\n2. First resume: azx_init_chip() is called with chip->initialized=1, so it returns early without re-initializing CORB/RIRB!\n3. The fix should distinguish between clearing the flag due to successful communication versus clearing it when exiting PM mode. We need to only clear the reset flag when there's no error, and separately handle the PM case. Looking at the condition more carefully, the error handling at line 233 only triggers when NOT in PM mode—if we're in PM and hit an error, we skip the reset logic entirely but still clear the flag, which masks the problem. should be that we're clearing the flag unconditionally when we shouldn't. The response_reset flag tracks whether a bus reset was needed, and it should only be cleared when we've actually recovered from an error or confirmed there's no error to handle. If we're in PM and skip error handling, the flag state is ambiguous—we haven't confirmed recovery, so clearing it seems wrong.\n\nThe fix might be simpler: only clear response_reset when err is actually zero, meaning no error occurred. This way, if an error happens during PM and gets skipped, the flag remains set to reflect that unhandled state. But that creates another problem—if we're stuck in PM with an error, the flag never gets cleared even after exiting PM.\n\nThe real issue might be earlier in the flow. If codec->in_pm isn't being cleared properly after resume completes, or if it's being set at the wrong time, then the error recovery path gets bypassed when it shouldn't be. Looking at hda_call_codec_resume(), the flag is set before resume and cleared after, but if something fails between those points, the state becomes inconsistent.\n\nGiven this is a regression between versions, the most likely cause is how the codec communication recovery interacts with the PM flag—either the flag isn't being managed correctly during resume, or the error handling logic changed in a way that breaks recovery when PM is involved. Looking at the error handling path in azx_rirb_get_response(), when a timeout triggers the switch to single_cmd mode at line 954, azx_free_cmd_io() gets called to disable the ringbuffer DMAs. If this occurs during resume with codec->in_pm set, the CORB/RIRB gets torn down while the codec is still in power management mode, potentially leaving the hardware in an inconsistent state that persists after resume completes.\n\nThe sequence appears to be: timeout during resume → single_cmd mode activated and CORB/RIRB disabled → resume finishes → subsequent audio operations fail because the ringbuffer remains disabled and won't be reinitialized since single_cmd mode is now active. On the next resume cycle, the chip->single_cmd flag remains set, perpetuating the problem.\n\nThe root cause is that once single_cmd gets set to 1 after an error, it persists across suspend/resume cycles. The initialization code at line 1222 skips cmd_io setup when single_cmd is already enabled, so the disabled CORB/RIRB never get restored. The solution is to reset chip->single_cmd = 0 during resume to force proper reinitialization of the command interface, ensuring the ringbuffers are functional Here's what I found:\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe bug is a **state persistence issue** across suspend/resume cycles in `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`:\n\n1. **Initial Problem**: When a codec communication timeout occurs (which can happen during normal initialization or under certain hardware conditions), the error recovery code in `azx_rirb_get_response()` progressively tries fallback mechanisms:\n   - Polling mode\n   - Disabling MSI\n   - Finally switching to \"single command mode\" (line 951) by setting `chip->single_cmd = 1`\n\n2. **The Bug**: Once `chip->single_cmd` is set to 1, it **never gets reset** on subsequent suspend/resume cycles. \n\n3. **Impact on Resume**: In `azx_resume()`, the function calls `azx_init_chip()`. However, `azx_init_chip()` contains this check at line 1222:\n   ```c\n   if (!chip->single_cmd)\n       azx_init_cmd_io(chip);\n   ```\n   Since `single_cmd` is still 1 from the previous error, **CORB/RIRB are not reinitialized**, leaving the hardware in an inconsistent state.\n\n4. **Result**: Codec communication fails with the timeout errors and error recovery code keeps triggering, resulting in choppy audio with 2-second silences.\n\n### Files and Functions Involved\n\n- **`sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`**:\n  - `azx_rirb_get_response()` (line 863): Sets `single_cmd = 1` on error\n  - `azx_resume()` (line 2539): Doesn't reset `single_cmd` before reinitializing\n  - `azx_init_chip()` (line 1209): Skips CORB/RIRB init if `single_cmd` is true\n\nThe fix requires resetting `chip->single_cmd = 0` in the resume path before calling `azx_init_chip()`, or ensuring proper reinitialization regardless of the single_cmd state."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":687,"cache_read_input_tokens":94284,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":687},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"25082372-81a3-4143-88fb-cce3b7f65b44","uuid":"2cf48e4a-6085-4e1f-8048-3be7fc303e6e"}

Let me create a summary of my findings:\n\n## Summary\n\nI've analyzed the HDA Intel sound driver bug that manifests as choppy audio after suspend to RAM in Linux kernel v3.7.6. Here's what I found:\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe bug is a **state persistence issue** across suspend/resume cycles in `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`:\n\n1. **Initial Problem**: When a codec communication timeout occurs (which can happen during normal initialization or under certain hardware conditions), the error recovery code in `azx_rirb_get_response()` progressively tries fallback mechanisms:\n   - Polling mode\n   - Disabling MSI\n   - Finally switching to \"single command mode\" (line 951) by setting `chip->single_cmd = 1`\n\n2. **The Bug**: Once `chip->single_cmd` is set to 1, it **never gets reset** on subsequent suspend/resume cycles. \n\n3. **Impact on Resume**: In `azx_resume()`, the function calls `azx_init_chip()`. However, `azx_init_chip()` contains this check at line 1222:\n   ```c\n   if (!chip->single_cmd)\n       azx_init_cmd_io(chip);\n   ```\n   Since `single_cmd` is still 1 from the previous error, **CORB/RIRB are not reinitialized**, leaving the hardware in an inconsistent state.\n\n4. **Result**: Codec communication fails with the timeout errors and error recovery code keeps triggering, resulting in choppy audio with 2-second silences.\n\n### Files and Functions Involved\n\n- **`sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`**:\n  - `azx_rirb_get_response()` (line 863): Sets `single_cmd = 1` on error\n  - `azx_resume()` (line 2539): Doesn't reset `single_cmd` before reinitializing\n  - `azx_init_chip()` (line 1209): Skips CORB/RIRB init if `single_cmd` is true\n\nThe fix requires resetting `chip->single_cmd = 0` in the resume path before calling `azx_init_chip()`, or ensuring proper reinitialization regardless of the single_cmd state.","stop_reason":null,"session_id":"25082372-81a3-4143-88fb-cce3b7f65b44","total_cost_usd":0.39067635,"usage":{"input_tokens":359,"cache_creation_input_tokens":68107,"cache_read_input_tokens":2306286,"output_tokens":14911,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":68107,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"},"modelUsage":{"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001":{"inputTokens":359,"outputTokens":14911,"cacheReadInputTokens":2306286,"cacheCreationInputTokens":68107,"webSearchRequests":0,"costUSD":0.39067635,"contextWindow":200000,"maxOutputTokens":32000}},"permission_denials":[],"fast_mode_state":"off","uuid":"ef9aebfb-1875-40b8-aaf3-46e7e8e8d128"}
